bash-4.4$ cut -d',' -f20,21 "Global YouTube Statistics.csv" | tail -n +2 | sort | uniq -c | sort -nr | head -3 | awk '{print $3, $2, "with", $1, "channels"}'
 2006,Mar with 15 channels
 2014,Jul with 13 channels
 2014,Aug with 12 channels
### Task 2 (Top 3 Channels)
This command uses:
'cut' to extract specific columns from the CSV file.

The -d',' option specifies the delimiter as a comma

'-f20,21' selects columns 20 and 21, which likely contain the "created_year" and "created_month" data.

'tail -n +2': This command skips the first line of the output, which likely contains column headers, and starts from the second line. This is because the first line usually contains headers in CSV files.

'sort': This command sorts the output alphabetically. It's likely used to prepare the data for the uniq command.

'uniq -c': This command finds unique occurrences of each combination of month and year and counts their frequency.

'sort -nr': This command sorts the output numerically in reverse order, arranging the combinations of month and year with the highest frequency at the top.

'head -3': This command selects the top three combinations with the highest frequency.

"awk '{print $3, $2, "with", $1, "channels"}'": This command formats and prints the output. It rearranges the columns to put the year first, then the month, followed by "with," the channel count, and "channels". The reason for using awk here is to customize the output format.

### Question 5

### Task 6
The command 'ps aux' tells the computer to show a list of all the programs running right now.
It gives details like who's using each program, how much memory and CPU power it's using, and what command started it.
